    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

<span id="freeTextContainer14366058984999964080">Two Truths and a Lie. The girls played it all the time in their tiny cabin at Camp Nightingale. Vivian, Natalie, Allison, and first-time camper Emma Davis, the youngest of the group. The games ended when Emma sleepily watched the others sneak out of the cabin in the dead of night. The last she—or anyone—saw of them was Vivian closing the cabin door behind her, hushing Emma</span>
  <span id="freeText14366058984999964080" style="display:none">Two Truths and a Lie. The girls played it all the time in their tiny cabin at Camp Nightingale. Vivian, Natalie, Allison, and first-time camper Emma Davis, the youngest of the group. The games ended when Emma sleepily watched the others sneak out of the cabin in the dead of night. The last she—or anyone—saw of them was Vivian closing the cabin door behind her, hushing Emma with a finger pressed to her lips.<br /><br />Now a rising star in the New York art scene, Emma turns her past into paintings—massive canvases filled with dark leaves and gnarled branches that cover ghostly shapes in white dresses. The paintings catch the attention of Francesca Harris-White, the socialite and wealthy owner of Camp Nightingale. When Francesca implores her to return to the newly reopened camp as a painting instructor, Emma sees an opportunity to try to find out what really happened to her friends.<br /><br />Yet it's immediately clear that all is not right at Camp Nightingale. Already haunted by memories from fifteen years ago, Emma discovers a security camera pointed directly at her cabin, mounting mistrust from Francesca and, most disturbing of all, cryptic clues Vivian left behind about the camp's twisted origins. As she digs deeper, Emma finds herself sorting through lies from the past while facing threats from both man and nature in the present.<br /><br />And the closer she gets to the truth about Camp Nightingale, the more she realizes it may come at a deadly price.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14366058984999964080" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I can say with some degree of certainty that there won't be a sequel or spin-off. While I loved creating Camp Nightingale and the characters who inhab<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I can say with some degree of certainty that there won't be a sequel or spin-off. While I loved creating Camp Nightingale and the characters who inhabited it, I'm happy with how I ended things. Rather than go back, I look forward to exploring new plots, new characters and new locations.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

    </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2323810553" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5101036459154448327"><b>BREAKING NEWS!</b>: The Last Time I Lied has been picked up by Amazon Studios to be developed into a series. <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://www.amazonbookreview.com/post/ed193e31-f886-4e8e-8cf2-e8c9f6bbd0d9/riley-sager'>https://www.amazonbookreview.com/post...</a> <br/><br/><b>Two truths and a lie:<br/><br/>1. This book rocked. <br/>2. Riley Sager is a thriller writing phenom. <br/>3. I hate reading. <br/><br/>Pretty sure you’ve got me figured out.</b><br/><br/><b>
  <i>Disclaimer</i>
</b>: I get really really ridiculously excited about good thrillers now and tend to use an excess of exclamation points, so this is just a preemptive “please excuse my flabbergabbling.”<br/><br/>This is a true </span>
  <span id="freeText5101036459154448327" style="display:none"><b>BREAKING NEWS!</b>: The Last Time I Lied has been picked up by Amazon Studios to be developed into a series. <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.amazonbookreview.com/post/ed193e31-f886-4e8e-8cf2-e8c9f6bbd0d9/riley-sager">https://www.amazonbookreview.com/post...</a> <br /><br /><b>Two truths and a lie:<br /><br />1. This book rocked. <br />2. Riley Sager is a thriller writing phenom. <br />3. I hate reading. <br /><br />Pretty sure you’ve got me figured out.</b><br /><br /><b>
  <i>Disclaimer</i>
</b>: I get really really ridiculously excited about good thrillers now and tend to use an excess of exclamation points, so this is just a preemptive “please excuse my flabbergabbling.”<br /><br />This is a true thriller in the sense of the word - it’s thrilling with understated suspense and it will creep you out in the best way possible. <br /><br />So compulsively readable and intriguing, I could not put this one down until I knew how it ended. Oh the twists and the turns and the theories that I had, that were all wrong by the way! It’s also super cinematic - I could totally see this one being turned into a film. <br /><br />Riley Sager has weaved an intoxicating tale of girls gone missing at a sleep away camp. There is a huge cast of characters, none of which you will trust, and a highly unreliable narrator. <br /><br />I loved how every flashback chapter was an answer to the question the previous chapter put forward. Everything was connected. You had all the pieces but no answers and had to figure it all out with the main character. <br /><br />The best kind of stories are the ones that can scare you silly without any violence. And that is exactly what you will find here. <br /><br />There is one teensy tiny detail of the conclusion that I have a question about and I need to discuss further. Riley Sager, shoot me an email so we can discuss!<br /><br />4.5 super creepy stars!<br /><br />Thank you to Dutton Books for my review copy! This was a buddy read with the Traveling Sisters - Berit, Brenda, Holly B, Mackenzie and Marialyce. Loved that you were all as equally enthusiastic about this one as I was!</span>

<div id="review_2341728855" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2341728855" />
    <a title="j e w e l s" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/68216634-j-e-w-e-l-s"><img alt="j e w e l s" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1552606306p2/68216634.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2341728855?book_show_action=true">Mar 27, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="j e w e l s" class="user" itemprop="url" name="j e w e l s" href="/user/show/68216634-j-e-w-e-l-s">j e w e l s</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68216634-j-e-w-e-l-s?shelf=twister-hall-of-fame">twister-hall-of-fame</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68216634-j-e-w-e-l-s?shelf=books-bejeweled">books-bejeweled</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2341728855" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14966316494680176868"><b>FIVE STARS</b><br/><br/>I’m trying my best to contain my excitement and review Riley Sager’s new book in a professional manner.<br/><br/><b>YIPPEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEE!</b><br/><br/>See that? I only used one exclamation point. I want at least 300 more! It is a spanking good, cracker jack of a novel that I could not stop reading for two days.<br/><br/><b>THE LAST TIME I LIED</b> is a brilliant and campy <i>(pun intended)</i> mystery for all you grown up fans of Nancy Drew or the Hardy Boys.<br/><br/><b>It will be the 2018 summer-beach-novel-must-read! This is a nostalgic and t</b></span>
  <span id="freeText14966316494680176868" style="display:none"><b>FIVE STARS</b><br /><br />I’m trying my best to contain my excitement and review Riley Sager’s new book in a professional manner.<br /><br /><b>YIPPEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEEE!</b><br /><br />See that? I only used one exclamation point. I want at least 300 more! It is a spanking good, cracker jack of a novel that I could not stop reading for two days.<br /><br /><b>THE LAST TIME I LIED</b> is a brilliant and campy <i>(pun intended)</i> mystery for all you grown up fans of Nancy Drew or the Hardy Boys.<br /><br /><b>It will be the 2018 summer-beach-novel-must-read! This is a nostalgic and twisted look back at your own summer camp memories. It’s terrific fun!</b><br /><br />I'm crazy about Sager’s deceptively easy writing style. He breezes right through the telling of the story, all the while creating mood, atmosphere and the fun kind of dread you get in the pit of your stomach while watching a horror flick. The pages suck you in and Sager holds your hand as he walks you through the creepy story that began 15 years ago at Camp Nightingale. <br /><br />Three out of four girls disappeared from the Dogwood cabin and that fourth girl? She suffered a nervous breakdown in the months following the disappearance of her friends. In a way, she is the SOLE SURVIVOR, and if you loved <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32796253.Final_Girls" title="Final Girls by Riley Sager" rel="nofollow noopener">Final Girls</a> you know what that means. Yes, Emma is a Final Girl and she is a sympathetic and very unreliable narrator. Emma has a chance to return to the camp fifteen years later, and of course, in Riley Sager’s world, she goes back to teach art at the camp. Oh, and to solve the old mystery while confronting her many demons. <br /><br />Please don’t bother to read the overly long and convoluted book jacket synopsis. It almost scared me away. So many names that are meaningless until you read the story. If you liked <b>FINAL GIRLS</b>, you will love <b>THE LAST TIME I LIED.</b> It is also delicious reading for fans of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/35356382.The_Chalk_Man" title="The Chalk Man by C.J. Tudor" rel="nofollow noopener">The Chalk Man</a> or <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25365530.Good_Me__Bad_Me" title="Good Me, Bad Me by Ali Land" rel="nofollow noopener">Good Me, Bad Me</a>.<br /><br /><b>THE LAST TIME I LIED is not going to be published until July 2018, I'm sorry to say. However---it is sooooooo worth the wait! It’s a completely different story from FINAL GIRLS, but the same brilliant author supervising the fun.</b><br /><br /><i>Many thanks to Dutton Publishers and Edelweiss for giving me the opportunity to read and review this book. All opinions are my own.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="14966316494680176868" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2435556753" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2435556753" />
    <a title="Chelsea Humphrey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/47207032-chelsea-humphrey"><img alt="Chelsea Humphrey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585613513p2/47207032.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2435556753?book_show_action=true">Jun 25, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chelsea Humphrey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chelsea Humphrey" href="/user/show/47207032-chelsea-humphrey">Chelsea Humphrey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781524743079" href="/book/show/36750068-the-last-time-i-lied">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Chelsea by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/2925586-dutton">Dutton</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47207032-chelsea-humphrey?shelf=from-publisher">from-publisher</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2435556753" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13768205460055956537"><i>This is how it begins.</i><br/><br/>I'll admit, I wasn't as intoxicated with <i>Final Girls</i> last year as the general public seemed to be, but I was in tune enough to realize that Riley Sager has some serious talent in his writing repertoire. His stories are darkly compulsive, and I've come to find that his growth in the psychological thriller field is enormous between his first book (good) and his second one (great). This is <b>EXACTLY</b> what I like to see in an author's pattern of book releases, and I honestly could</span>
  <span id="freeText13768205460055956537" style="display:none"><i>This is how it begins.</i><br /><br />I'll admit, I wasn't as intoxicated with <i>Final Girls</i> last year as the general public seemed to be, but I was in tune enough to realize that Riley Sager has some serious talent in his writing repertoire. His stories are darkly compulsive, and I've come to find that his growth in the psychological thriller field is enormous between his first book (good) and his second one (great). This is <b>EXACTLY</b> what I like to see in an author's pattern of book releases, and I honestly couldn't be more excited for where his next work takes us.<br /><br /><i>You see the fine grains of the pine plank wall, smell the traces of campfire smoke in your hair, and know exactly where you are. Camp Nightingale.</i><br /><br />I would say the format of storytelling is similar to <i>Final Girls</i>, and both books are dark psychological thrillers, but the similarities end there. Where the previous novel was more of a slasher thriller with a YA vibe, this one was a more grown up, complex psychological thriller that was driven by the multiple mysteries at hand. While I can't put my finger on exactly what it is that I liked more about <i>The Last Time I Lied</i>, I think it had something to do with the timing of reading it, plus the fact that this one felt far less formulaic and engaged my brain power as a reader, rather than just expecting me to sit back and be entertained alone. <br /><br /><i>So much water. So much land. So many places to disappear.</i><br /><br />It's tricky to go into details without spoiling any of the book, but it's definitely one that will grasp your attention from the prologue. The story is told alternating between flashbacks during Emma's first stay at Camp Nightingale and present day, which is 15 years in the future. What looks like a straightforward investigation into the disappearance of Emma's three friends from the past turns into a hella good suspenseful romp into so many different directions that I had to re-read one of the reveal sections <b>FOUR TIMES</b> before I could move forward because- <i>Sager fooled me</i>! As an avid suspense aficionado, it's a feeling that I don't get often these days and cherish when the opportunity comes along. <br /><br /><i>You think of all these things and begin to scream.</i><br /><br />I'm still torn on how I feel about a few aspects of the ending, but overall I was very pleased with each facet of this one. It was entertaining, engaging, and had that "unputdownable" factor we have all come to crave from our latest read. If you've been eagerly anticipating this one as much as I have over the past year, I hope you're as satisfied with the pay off as I was. At a time that I've been almost ready to give up on psychological thrillers, I am so thrilled to have consumed this one and for it redeeming the genre in my eyes and persuading me to ride the suspense train a little bit longer. <br /><br /><i>* I received a review copy from the publisher. </i></span>
  <a data-text-id="13768205460055956537" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2268089590" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2268089590" />
    <a title="megs_bookrack" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48328025-megs-bookrack"><img alt="megs_bookrack" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532027727p2/48328025.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2268089590?book_show_action=true">Apr 20, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="megs_bookrack" class="user" itemprop="url" name="megs_bookrack" href="/user/show/48328025-megs-bookrack">megs_bookrack</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48328025-megs-bookrack?shelf=arcs-read">arcs-read</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2268089590" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer7253363145516894701"><b>Riley Sager, I love you.</b> <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1471187045ra/20010096.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b><i>The Last Time I Lied</i> was thrilling from beginning to end.</b> It kept me guessing until the final pages and I certainly didn't see THAT ending coming.<br/><br/>On her first day at Camp Nightingale, Emma was late; her parents doing. Subsequently, as luck would have it, she got stuck in a cabin with girls much older than herself. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1552938503ra/27225709.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Luckily, her pretty and popular bunkmate, Vivian, took Emma under her wing. <br/><br/>Soon she was having a camp experience unlike any of the other girls her age.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1552938503ra/27225710.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>The tim</span>
  <span id="freeText7253363145516894701" style="display:none"><b>Riley Sager, I love you.</b> <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1471187045ra/20010096.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b><i>The Last Time I Lied</i> was thrilling from beginning to end.</b> It kept me guessing until the final pages and I certainly didn't see THAT ending coming.<br><br>On her first day at Camp Nightingale, Emma was late; her parents doing. Subsequently, as luck would have it, she got stuck in a cabin with girls much older than herself. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1552938503ra/27225709.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Luckily, her pretty and popular bunkmate, Vivian, took Emma under her wing. <br><br>Soon she was having a camp experience unlike any of the other girls her age.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1552938503ra/27225710.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The time passes as time at summer camp does, until the 4th of July, when Emma's three bunkmates disappear, never to be seen again.<br><br>Fifteen years later, Emma, continues to be haunted by the experience. Now a successful artist in New York City, she melds the haunting images of her camp experience into her work. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1528638575ra/25709680.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Unexpectedly invited back to Camp Nightingale by the wealthy owner, Franny Harris-White, to be an art instructor, Emma accepts. <br><br>Although returning to the location of her trauma gives her pause, she feels compelled to return.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1578327536ra/28724580.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>She hopes with her time there, she can finally piece together what happened to her friends on that night long ago.<br><br>Once at camp, she is reunited with many faces from her past, including the handsome Theo, Emma's crush from THAT summer. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1518883944ra/25077710.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This story is <b>darkly atmospheric</b> and filled with mystery and dread. <br><br>Sager's writing extremely vivid. As I am reading, I have the entire drama unfolding in my mind with the clarity of a movie. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1509892941ra/24368229.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I felt the same way with <i>Final Girls</i>. His descriptions and feelings are so easy to follow and imagine; they're definitely one of my favorite things about his writing. <br><br>As the story unfolds, there are multiple occasions where you think you know what happened all those years ago, but those thoughts are quickly dashed away by new information coming forth. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1491002959ra/22368056.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The cast of characters was fantastic and both timelines unfolded with such ease and excitement, it made this novel a very quick read. <br><br>I have absolutely nothing negative to say. <b>I loved it, would read it again and would recommend to any Thriller reader</b>. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1498786214ra/23162007.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I cannot wait to see what Sager comes up with next. <br><br>You better believe I will be waiting for it and promptly buying it upon release!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1505168204ra/23893411.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Thank you so much to the publisher, Dutton Press, for providing me with a copy of this book to read and review. <br><br>It was a highlight of my year, for sure, and I greatly appreciate the opportunity!</span>

<div id="review_2360138014" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2360138014" />
    <a title="Emma Giordano" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30604861-emma-giordano"><img alt="Emma Giordano" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1569693958p2/30604861.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2360138014?book_show_action=true">Oct 03, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma Giordano" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma Giordano" href="/user/show/30604861-emma-giordano">Emma Giordano</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30604861-emma-giordano?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2360138014" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14346986736113077100">2.5 Stars. I’m honestly so conflicted on this book that I don’t even want to write a review because I’m not really sure where my thoughts are. Did I like it at all? Did I absolutely hate it? I honestly can’t tell you.<br/><br/>CW: violence, drowning, peeping toms, cancer, schizophreniform<br/><br/>While I enjoyed Riley Sager’s previous work, <i>Final Girls</i>, I had some issues with the writing. While I do feel that many of those issues were resolved in <i>The Last Time I Lied</i>, I actually prefer <i>Final Girls</i>. <i>Final Girls</i> was</span>
  <span id="freeText14346986736113077100" style="display:none">2.5 Stars. I’m honestly so conflicted on this book that I don’t even want to write a review because I’m not really sure where my thoughts are. Did I like it at all? Did I absolutely hate it? I honestly can’t tell you.<br /><br />CW: violence, drowning, peeping toms, cancer, schizophreniform<br /><br />While I enjoyed Riley Sager’s previous work, <i>Final Girls</i>, I had some issues with the writing. While I do feel that many of those issues were resolved in <i>The Last Time I Lied</i>, I actually prefer <i>Final Girls</i>. <i>Final Girls</i> was intriguing to me as it is a twist on a famous trope in horror, whereas <i>The Last Time I Lied</i> is fairly similar to many thrillers out there. I do think <i>The Last Time I Lied</i> is a better constructed novel, but I wasn’t all that entertained by this story. By the end, I was finishing it just to finish it.<br /><br />None of the characters stood out to me. I felt almost all of them were characters I’ve read before. Excluding Emma, I found few characters to be well-developed and have a multitude of motivations. Vivian is the only notable character, but I wouldn’t consider that a compliment as the only reason she stands out is because she’s an overly-sexualized teenager written entirely through a male-gaze. She made me uncomfortable, and not in the way you want to be uncomfortable while reading a thriller.<br /><br />Also, the theme of “lying” was shoved down my throat so much, it was suffocating. We get it. ~Everyone lies so we can’t trust any of the characters.~ It’s like the author thinks readers aren’t capable of figuring that out themselves. I was so over the blatant attention to lies at the very beginning of the work.<br /><br />Many of the positive reviews of this novel mention the “shocking, twist ending” and I concur – the very last moments of this book caught me off guard. But it personally was not enough to save a story I didn’t fully enjoy otherwise.<br /><br />I’m aware I’m the unpopular opinion for this book, but it wasn’t a great read for me. I can’t for the life of me tell you why, but I’ll probably give Riley Sager another try in the future. I guess that says something about his ability to draw in readers.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14346986736113077100" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2434763294" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2434763294" />
    <a title="BernLuvsBooks " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3087404-bernluvsbooks"><img alt="BernLuvsBooks " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585010050p2/3087404.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2434763294?book_show_action=true">Jun 26, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="BernLuvsBooks " class="user" itemprop="url" name="BernLuvsBooks " href="/user/show/3087404-bernluvsbooks">BernLuvsBooks </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3087404-bernluvsbooks?shelf=fave-reads">fave-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3087404-bernluvsbooks?shelf=2018">2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3087404-bernluvsbooks?shelf=adult-reads">adult-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3087404-bernluvsbooks?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2434763294" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer502717664792233706">🚣🏻‍♀️ <b> <i> 5 Stars for Riley Sager’s campy summer mystery - The Last Time I Lied </i></b>  🏕<br/><br/>I was uneasy the entire time I read this book. Part of that was my own excited expectations/anticipation of the book but the other part was Sager’s writing. <b> He knows how to create an elusive mood that leaves you full of dread, yet wanting more. </b> You’re reading, turning page after page, just waiting for “that something” to happen. You know it’s coming. You’re creeped out and suspicious of everyone. You can’t put the</span>
  <span id="freeText502717664792233706" style="display:none">🚣🏻‍♀️ <b> <i> 5 Stars for Riley Sager’s campy summer mystery - The Last Time I Lied </i></b>  🏕<br /><br />I was uneasy the entire time I read this book. Part of that was my own excited expectations/anticipation of the book but the other part was Sager’s writing. <b> He knows how to create an elusive mood that leaves you full of dread, yet wanting more. </b> You’re reading, turning page after page, just waiting for “that something” to happen. You know it’s coming. You’re creeped out and suspicious of everyone. You can’t put the book down because you simply have to know where its all going. That’s my reading experience with this book in a nutshell and I loved every minute of it. <br /><br />Sager masterfully spun a tale that is told in two different times - the present &amp; past (told via flashback from 15 years ago). It all began at Camp Nightingale 15 years prior when three girls disappear from Dogwood cabin. Emma, the youngest of the four girls rooming in the cabin was the only one left. She is deeply affected by the disappearance of her friends and is haunted by the girls throughout her life. Emma is unable to come to terms with the terrible tragedy because they never fully learned what happened to the girls that fateful summer night. <br /><br />Flash forward 15 years and Camp Nightingale is once again opening its doors to campers. Emma has been invited to teach art at the camp for the summer and of course she accepts. It’s her chance to finally solve the mystery and hopefully put the events of that summer behind her. <br /><br />Emma is a wonderfully sympathetic yet unreliable narrator. Can her memories be trusted when she herself admits to having had a nervous breakdown in the months after her first camp experience? There were so many secrets that it was nearly impossible to figure out what was true and what wasn’t. There were so many well crafted layers to this mystery! I literally suspected everyone, trusted no one &amp; still had it all wrong in the end. I LOVE when I don’t see "it" coming. It was all there, the crumbs had been woven into the story but with Emma being such an unreliable narrator you simply don’t know what to think or who to believe. <br /><br /><b> The book had me riveted from beginning to end. </b> I too was on a search for the truth with Emma amidst all the secrets, lies &amp; guilt. I definitely recommend this read to fellow mystery fans and hope it will keep you second guessing just as it did me!<br /><br /><i> <u> The Last Time I Lied </u></i>  has even been picked up by Amazon Studios to be adapted into a limited series!!! Yay, I can't wait!!!!!  You can read all about it here if you'd like --&gt; <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.amazonbookreview.com/post/ed193e31-f886-4e8e-8cf2-e8c9f6bbd0d9/riley-sager">https://www.amazonbookreview.com/post...</a> <br /><br /><b> <i> Thank you to NetGalley, Dutton, Penguin Books, and Riley Sager for an advanced copy of this book in exchange for an honest review. </i></b> </span>
  <a data-text-id="502717664792233706" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2330621516" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2330621516" />
    <a title="Debra" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5032725-debra"><img alt="Debra" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1525132364p2/5032725.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2330621516?book_show_action=true">May 10, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Debra" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Debra" href="/user/show/5032725-debra">Debra</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5032725-debra?shelf=edelweiss">edelweiss</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2330621516" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4378275179419890841">4.5 stars<br/><br/>While reading my second book by Sager, I can't help but think that he is an 80's horror movie fan or at least grew up in the 80's watching these flicks. His other book, "Final Girls" read like an 80's horror film to me (which I loved!) and while reading The Last Time I Lied, I felt as if I was at Camp Crystal Lake....oops...I meant at Camp Nightingale. And no, there is no killer in a hockey mask chasing camp counselors through the woods here, but it does have a camp in the middle of the</span>
  <span id="freeText4378275179419890841" style="display:none">4.5 stars<br /><br />While reading my second book by Sager, I can't help but think that he is an 80's horror movie fan or at least grew up in the 80's watching these flicks. His other book, "Final Girls" read like an 80's horror film to me (which I loved!) and while reading The Last Time I Lied, I felt as if I was at Camp Crystal Lake....oops...I meant at Camp Nightingale. And no, there is no killer in a hockey mask chasing camp counselors through the woods here, but it does have a camp in the middle of the woods, where campers tell each other rumors about the camp’s dark history. Is there any truth to these rumors or are the girls just trying to scare each other?<br /><br />When Emma was thirteen years old her parents sent her to "camp rich bitch" a.k.a. Camp Nightingale. Since she arrived late, she is placed in a cabin called Dogwood with three older teens: Vivian, Allison, and Natalie. One-night Emma wakes to see the trio sneaking out and is told she is to0 young to go with them. The three teens are never seen again. <br /><br />Fifteen years later, Emma is an artist who cannot stop drawing the images of the missing girls in her artwork. She is still haunted by that summer and the events which led up to the disappearance of the missing teens. When the camp owner, Francesca Harris-White, invites her to return to the camp for its re-opening, Emma is torn but eventually agrees to teach art lessons at the camp. Emma hopes this will help her move on and come to terms with the events of that summer and the disappearance of her bunk mates.<br /><br />From the start, things don't seem to be going according to plan. Emma is back in the cabin she shared with the missing girls fifteen years ago. This is only the beginning. Searching for the truth, she stumbles upon some clues left behind by one of the girls. Someone must not have warned her to "be careful what you wish/look for” What happens when what you've been searching for, comes looking for you? Will finding the truth set her free or make things worse? Can you ever go back again? YES, she does go back ...but you know what I mean. <br /><br />A lot of characters have secrets in this book - I loved this! The cabin mates loved to play "two truths and a lie". I felt as if I were playing that game right along with them, trying to decipher what was real, what was a lie, who is lying (if anyone), who is being deceptive, who is reliable, etc. This was a fun and creepy (yes things can be fun and creepy at the same time!) jaunt through the woods! Ahhh, I could hear the twigs breaking underfoot, see the ripples in the lake and hear the birds chirping. What I couldn't do was find those missing "mean girls." I dare you..no wait..I triple dog dare you to try and figure this book out! If you do, then you are a better super sleuth that I am! I pinkie promise you that this book delivers on a few twist and turns.<br /><br />There are a lot of characters in this book, but I never found this to be confusing. I found it easy to keep track of everyone. Some of the characters are likable, some not so much, some are mean, some seem too syrupy sweet, some will seem deceptive and some you may not trust. I love how he draw them to stir the plot and keep the reader guessing.<br /><br />At first this book did seem a little slow to me, mainly because I wanted to be instantly grabbed by this book as I was Final Girls. But I found as I kept reading, I became hooked. Going back and forth in time, looking for clues, I was invested in learning what happened. I felt for characters and was suspicious of them, and then a character would do something or say something and then I suspected them. Thus, I was intrigued and HAD to know whodunit! The woods, cabin and lake were the perfect back drop for this riveting book about missing girls, the search for the truth, the pains of growing up, and the guilt of lies.<br /><br />I received a copy of this book from Dutton Publishing and Edelweiss in exchange for an honest review.<br /><br />See more of my reviews at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.openbookpost.com">www.openbookpost.com</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="4378275179419890841" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Meredith" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30978160-meredith"><img alt="Meredith" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1423329725p2/30978160.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2450767250?book_show_action=true">Jul 13, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Meredith" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Meredith" href="/user/show/30978160-meredith">Meredith</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30978160-meredith?shelf=edelweiss">edelweiss</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2450767250" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16402440691117050832"><br/><b>
  <i>“Sometimes a lie is more than just a lie. Sometimes it’s the only way to win.”</i>
</b><br/><br/>Picture this: Sleepaway camp. 4 girls share a cabin until the day 3 disappear never to be found. One 13-year-old girl is left to tell their story. But her stories are built around lies.<br/><br/>15 years later, the same girl returns to the camp to teach art and assist the owner’s new charitable endeavor. She is assigned to the same cabin that the girls disappeared from. Once again, 3 girls go missing. Something is amiss at C</span>
  <span id="freeText16402440691117050832" style="display:none"><br /><b>
  <i>“Sometimes a lie is more than just a lie. Sometimes it’s the only way to win.”</i>
</b><br /><br />Picture this: Sleepaway camp. 4 girls share a cabin until the day 3 disappear never to be found. One 13-year-old girl is left to tell their story. But her stories are built around lies.<br /><br />15 years later, the same girl returns to the camp to teach art and assist the owner’s new charitable endeavor. She is assigned to the same cabin that the girls disappeared from. Once again, 3 girls go missing. Something is amiss at Camp Nightingale.<br /><br /><i>The Last Time I Lied</i> is a tension-packed, atmospheric thriller! Sager brings Camp Nightingale to life: from the eerie camp grounds, to the mysterious lake, to the campfire smoke, to the angst of the teenage campers, I was transported. <b>This element of the novel felt so real and made this book for me! </b><br /><br />While things start off a little slow, I was interested enough in the mystery to keep on reading. Bits and pieces are gradually revealed, dark twists and turns occur, culminating in an over-the-top ending. While this element would normally have taken me out of a book, in this instance, it had me smiling (in a good way)! <b>Overall, The Last Time I Lied was a fun, suspenseful read that left me wanting more!</b><br /><br />I received a copy of this book from Edelweiss+ and Dutton, Penguin Books in exchange for an honest review. </span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2204364868" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer8808921324124612563"><b>I just finished my reread of this book and it was so freaking good.</b> I think this time around I'd bump it up to a 4.5 rating (the first time around I rated it 4 stars). There were so many plot twists I had forgotten about which made this reread so fun and exciting, and I absolutely LOVE the spooky camp vibes. Everything I enjoyed about it the first time I just enjoyed it even more the second time. I love the complicated teenage girl friendships and the unreliable narrator in Emma, and this time a</span>
  <span id="freeText8808921324124612563" style="display:none"><b>I just finished my reread of this book and it was so freaking good.</b> I think this time around I'd bump it up to a 4.5 rating (the first time around I rated it 4 stars). There were so many plot twists I had forgotten about which made this reread so fun and exciting, and I absolutely LOVE the spooky camp vibes. Everything I enjoyed about it the first time I just enjoyed it even more the second time. I love the complicated teenage girl friendships and the unreliable narrator in Emma, and this time around reading that ending I found it to be more ambiguous??? So I was shook by that. I just think Riley Sager is one of the best thriller authors and his writing is just so addicting and so easy to get sucked into the story. I really really enjoyed this one, I still think Lock Every Door is my all time favorite but wow all his books are just so freaking good. <br /><br /><b>ORIGINAL REVIEW</b>:<br />Ahhh so good! I liked this one more than Final Girls! This book was so creepy and eerie and it kept me guessing until the last page! I’m so surprised by all the plot twists! I don’t have time to write a full review but here are some thoughts: <br /><br />-I read this on the plane and in the hotel room I couldn’t put it down<br />-Giving me Gone Girl vibes with the diaries<br />-So intense I still didn’t guess the ending<br />-Love the main character and her unreliable narrating<br />-Love how sections of this book are told in second person, makes it even creepier<br />-Love the atmosphere of the creepy haunted camp in the middle of the woods<br />-Some parts of this felt paranormal or something which I really enjoyed<br />-Love the way this book really studies teenage girl friendships and how intense they can be. Kind of reminds me of Dangerous Girls<br />-Loved the main theme of two truths and a lie and how that really gets tied in a lot throughout the story! It even had me guessing what was real and what was a lie<br />-Amazing writing! That ending though! I enjoyed this one even more than Final Girls</span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2661287360" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer12850819922438449528"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1551534793i/27143282._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>This was my first book from Riley Sager, and I definitely want to read more from him. The Last Time I Lied is my first 5 stars book in 2019. <b> Absolutely one of my favorite thriller. </b><br/><br/>The plot has everything that's gripping the reader; creepy summer camp in the woods, vanished girls, lot of dirty secrets, and more lies. Everything started 15 years ago when 4 girls shared one cabin in Camp Nightingale. But one night three of them vanished. Emma nowadays is a painter and returns to the camp as an in</span>
  <span id="freeText12850819922438449528" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1551534793i/27143282._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This was my first book from Riley Sager, and I definitely want to read more from him. The Last Time I Lied is my first 5 stars book in 2019. <b> Absolutely one of my favorite thriller. </b><br><br>The plot has everything that's gripping the reader; creepy summer camp in the woods, vanished girls, lot of dirty secrets, and more lies. Everything started 15 years ago when 4 girls shared one cabin in Camp Nightingale. But one night three of them vanished. Emma nowadays is a painter and returns to the camp as an instructor to find out what happened 15 years ago. Who knows... <br>The book has two timelines, one is in the present and the other is in the past. This gave me constant stress, Riley Sager did a great job. I couldn't put it down!<br><br>I love the "two truths, one lie" game that the girls play in the whole story. I've never been able to decide which one is right. The pacing was really good. It was slow, but it was really tense.<br><br>I loved the main character Emma. She was unreliable, but I sympathize with her. What I loved the most was the camp atmosphere. It was so spooky! The camp was haunted at night, I was so scared when the girls walked out from their cabin in the middle of the night. I wouldn't have been there. Brrr.<br><br>The book's ending was shocking. I can't figure out what will happen. In the end were 3 big twist that I didn't expect at all. When I read it, I was so traumatized that I just blinked on my kindle for long minutes. I couldn't believe what happened! I love these types of endings.<br><br>This book is my new favorite. If you are looking for a gripping, exciting thriller please read this!</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17397952452260301562">Holy Shooty Balls this was a good one! 😝 I absolutely LOVED this book!<br/><br/>THE LAST TIME I LIED by RILEY SAGER was an absolutely fantastic, compulsive, thrilling, and tension filled psychological thriller that had me totally engaged and racing through those pages as fast as I could to see how this story was going to end.   <span id="freeText17397952452260301562" style="display:none">Holy Shooty Balls this was a good one! 😝 I absolutely LOVED this book!<br /><br />THE LAST TIME I LIED by RILEY SAGER was an absolutely fantastic, compulsive, thrilling, and tension filled psychological thriller that had me totally engaged and racing through those pages as fast as I could to see how this story was going to end. I was totally blown away with that absolutely shocking and surprise ending! I did another whoop at books end. <br /><br />RILEY SAGER delivers an extremely detailed, twisty, atmospheric and well-written story here. I absolutely love his writing style and the way that he set the mood was pretty much perfect for a creepy and thrilling reading experience for me. I had that uneasy and apprehensive feeling throughout most of this novel which I am always seeking from my thrillers. This one definitely delivered! <br /><br />This novel was so gripping and intriguing and in my opinion had the perfect setting. The creepy woods, cabin, and the eerie lake with the camp setting was so good. The camp setting had me reminiscing about my summer camp memories when I was younger. I couldn’t help thinking Nancy Drew or The Hardy Boys while I was reading this one too. Also, another fun aspect of this novel was the game “two truths and a lie” that the girls played at Camp Nightingale in their cabin. I’m not going to lie - I absolutely loved this book! Would highly recommend!<br /><br />Expected Publishing Date: July 10, 2018<br /><br />Thank you so much to Edelweiss, Dutton Publishing, and Riley Sager for the opportunity to read an advanced copy of this book.<br /><br />Review written and posted on our themed book blog Two Sisters Lost In A Coulee Reading.<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://twosisterslostinacoulee.com">https://twosisterslostinacoulee.com</a><br /><br />Coulee: a term applied rather loosely to different landforms, all of which refer to a kind of valley.</span>

    <a title="Mary Beth " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14233569-mary-beth"><img alt="Mary Beth " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1479858526p2/14233569.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2434644694?book_show_action=true">Jun 24, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mary Beth " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mary Beth " href="/user/show/14233569-mary-beth">Mary Beth </a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2434644694" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer16525368505064958769"><b>Five Solid Shiny Stars</b> <br/><br/>Emma Davis goes away to summer camp at Camp Nightingale. She shares a cabin with three other girls, Vivian, Natalie, and Alison. She learns how to play a game, Two Truths And A Lie. They play it All the time. All three girls disappear without a trace in the woods at night time. <br/><br/>Fifteen years later the camp reopens and Emma returns as a painting instructor and finds an opportunity to try to find out what really happened to her friends, that has haunted her. Emma is assigned</span>
  <span id="freeText16525368505064958769" style="display:none"><b>Five Solid Shiny Stars</b> <br /><br />Emma Davis goes away to summer camp at Camp Nightingale. She shares a cabin with three other girls, Vivian, Natalie, and Alison. She learns how to play a game, Two Truths And A Lie. They play it All the time. All three girls disappear without a trace in the woods at night time. <br /><br />Fifteen years later the camp reopens and Emma returns as a painting instructor and finds an opportunity to try to find out what really happened to her friends, that has haunted her. Emma is assigned to the same cabin she slept in as a teenager. She finds a security camera pointing<br /> directly at her cabin. She also finds the word liar in red paint on the front door. The closer she gets to the truth about Camp Nightingale, the more she realizes it may come at a deadly price.<br /><br />This book was a big surprise. Now I want to read Final Girls. This was a creepy spooky read. <br />This book goes back and forth from the past and present. It goes back 15 years ago, when Emma was a teenager to the present. <br />This is my favorite psychological thriller for this year. <br /><br />This book was done so well. It was a little dark but it wasn't graphic. It is a thriller with a little bit of horror. It is a phenomenal mystery. There are lots of twists and turns that will keep you on the edge of your seat. It kept me guessing and guessing, and the ending just shocked me. <br />I hooked straight from the beginning to the very end. The characters were done so well and I loved the writing style. <br />I highly recommend it.<br /><br />This was a Traveling Sister read and it was a great discussion which made this a great reading experience.<br /><br />I want to thank Edelweiss, Dutton, and Riley Sager for the copy of this book in exchange for a honest review.</span>

<div id="review_2427233380" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2427233380" />
    <a title="Mackenzie - PhDiva Books" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/57632045-mackenzie---phdiva-books"><img alt="Mackenzie - PhDiva Books" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1562505567p2/57632045.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2427233380?book_show_action=true">Jun 17, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mackenzie - PhDiva Books" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mackenzie - PhDiva Books" href="/user/show/57632045-mackenzie---phdiva-books">Mackenzie - PhDiva Books</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57632045-mackenzie---phdiva-books?shelf=2018-psychological-thrillers">2018-psychological-thrillers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57632045-mackenzie---phdiva-books?shelf=traveling-sisters">traveling-sisters</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2427233380" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15273921940609476494">Riley Sager somehow surpasses the amazing hype surrounding his first novel, <i>Final Girls</i>, with an absolutely compulsively-good psychological thriller full or secrets, lies, and shocking truths that you won’t be able to put down! <br/><br/>I have to say, I have read some outstanding books already in 2018, but this is by far the best psychological thriller for me this year! I was captivated by this book! I have a list of quotes and notes several pages long that I pulled while reading. Since I reached the sho</span>
  <span id="freeText15273921940609476494" style="display:none">Riley Sager somehow surpasses the amazing hype surrounding his first novel, <i>Final Girls</i>, with an absolutely compulsively-good psychological thriller full or secrets, lies, and shocking truths that you won’t be able to put down! <br /><br />I have to say, I have read some outstanding books already in 2018, but this is by far the best psychological thriller for me this year! I was captivated by this book! I have a list of quotes and notes several pages long that I pulled while reading. Since I reached the shocking ending (seriously! What an ending!!!), I have been going back to those quotes and notes and finding even more clues and meaning in them. <br /><br />We read this as a Traveling Sister read, and the discussion has been so engaging and wonderful. We each are finding clues that give us a new theory about aspects of the book. I wish I could share, but you should go in and experience this one as it is written! You will find your own path through the mysterious web of truth and lies, and I think this one will keep you guessing!!<br /><br /><b>About the Book</b><br /><br />Emma Davis was 13 years old when she first attended Camp Nightingale—a summer sleepaway camp for the upper-class girls of the northeastern states. Emma is late—her mother didn’t mention that she would be away all summer until the first day of camp—and so she is placed into a tiny cabin with popular senior campers Vivian, Natalie, and Allison. Emma immediately bonds with the beautiful, enigmatic Vivian. Vivian feels like the older sister Emma always wanted. The girls quickly engage Emma in their favorite game, two truths and a lie. The point of the game is to trick others into believing your lie. And then one night, Emma watches the girls sneak out of the cabin. By the next morning, they’ve disappeared for good, and Emma is left wondering if she could have stopped them.<br /><br /><i>
  <b>Two truths…</b>
</i><br /><br />At 28, Emma is a successful painter with a gallery full of her Forest series—paintings inspired by the forest at Camp Nightingale and her lingering questions around that summer. Not a day goes by that Emma doesn’t think about the three missing girls, particularly Vivian. And then Franny, the wealthy owner of Camp Nightingale, approaches Emma with an offer—return to Camp Nightingale’s grand re-opening. Emma thinks this may be her opportunity to finally process what happened to her friends and move on for good. But all is not as it seems once she arrives at Camp Nightingale. <br /><br /><i>
  <b>And a lie…</b>
</i><br /><br />But Emma has secrets she has never revealed to anyone. About that summer. About the girls. Emma may know more about what happened than she admits. Though Emma tries to live a life of truths, she can’t seem to escape her lies that summer. And it seems that someone out there knows what Emma lied about, and is trying to make Emma pay. Can Emma find the truth before her lies catch up to her?<br /><br /><b>Reflection</b><br /><br />I cannot put into words how wonderful this book is! It has layers upon layers of secrets, lies, and mystery that I continue to peel back, even after finishing. Small moments that seemed innocuous at first reading take on so much meaning as I discovered more about the events at Camp Nightingale. The characters are all slightly unsettling in a good way. You’re never totally sure that anyone is telling the full truth. But as Vivian says, lying is how you win the game.<br /><br />One of my absolute favorite things about this book was the mysterious setting of Camp Nightingale. Sager uses the setting as a character in and of itself. He says at one point, <i>“Like most old structures, there's a heaviness to the Lodge, a somberness. I think of all the years it's witnessed. All those seasons and storms and secrets...”</i> The description of a place as having a memory; of knowing all of the secrets, and it creating a personality to the building that may not exist if things had been different. Emma reflects at one point that she was getting reacquainted with the lake, only to then state that actually, it felt like the lake was getting reacquainted with her. And then at other times several characters mention the forest as inviting them in, and the pull it has for those at the camp. The setting of the book completely came alive through Sager’s wonderful writing. It became a force within the story that held the clues to the mystery, if only Emma could be brave enough to ask.<br /><br />And finally, THAT ENDING! I can’t say much more because I refuse to spoil even a second of this wonderful ending, but boy-oh-boy was I paging back and forward, processing what I just read. I can’t wait for readers to discover this book for themselves! The entire book is a masterpiece, and one I already am planning to read again. And like all of the best books, I already know that each time I read it, I’ll get a bit more out of it. <br /><br />Thank you so much to Dutton, Penguin Books, and Riley Sager for an advanced copy of this book in exchange for an honest review.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15273921940609476494" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer10583431341460554691"><b>6 Strikingly Stupendous Stars 🌟🌟🌟🌟🌟🌟</b><br/><br/>Yes six, seis, sexe,sechs,sei.... and I’m sure whatever language you choose to read this book in the result will be the same... it was just that fabulous!<br/><i><br/>Two truths and a lie...<br/><br/>1 I never gush over books!<br/>2 this was the best book I’ve read so far this year!!!<br/>3 Riley Sager is being added to my list of authors who I will autobuy/request.</i><br/><br/>I’m sure you figured it out... I am the queen of gushing! And this is a book that makes me want to shout from the rooftops! From </span>
  <span id="freeText10583431341460554691" style="display:none"><b>6 Strikingly Stupendous Stars 🌟🌟🌟🌟🌟🌟</b><br /><br />Yes six, seis, sexe,sechs,sei.... and I’m sure whatever language you choose to read this book in the result will be the same... it was just that fabulous!<br /><i><br />Two truths and a lie...<br /><br />1 I never gush over books!<br />2 this was the best book I’ve read so far this year!!!<br />3 Riley Sager is being added to my list of authors who I will autobuy/request.</i><br /><br />I’m sure you figured it out... I am the queen of gushing! And this is a book that makes me want to shout from the rooftops! From first page to last this book had me captivated... this is going to sound odd but I felt as though I was in a forest of browns and greens every time I pick this book up.... it was so atmospheric and descriptive that I felt as though I was there at camp with these girls... The forest, the lake, the tension was all drawn so well by Sager... I could smell the trees, feel the water, and I was on the edge of my seat throughout this entire book!<br /><br />Emma is a “final girl“ how appropriate is that? when she was at camp 15 years ago she was the only girl from her cabin to not disappear ... my only complaint of Sager’s previous book was I would have liked the psychology of these “final girls” to have been explored more in depth , so... what a treat this book was! Emma now a well respected artist paints these girls in all her paintings... she sees Vivian everywhere... and she cannot let go of the fact that she had something to do with their disappearance... that is all I am saying about the plot, I do not want to ruin this gem of a book for you...<br /><br />I am just so jealous of all of you who have not read this yet, what a treat you have in front of you! A campy book that will grab onto you and will not let go... a book filled with twists, Twists, and more twists, and just when you think you’ve got it all figured out..... an ending you will not see coming!<br /><br /><br /><br />Emphatically recommend this book, especially if you are a fan of the psychological thriller genre! If you liked “Final Girls you will love “The Last Time I Lied” and that is no lie!<br /><br />*** many thanks to Penguin Dutton for my copy of this book ***</span>

<div id="review_2430209910" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2430209910" />
    <a title="Christina - Recipe &amp; a Read" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24156068-christina---recipe-a-read"><img alt="Christina - Recipe &amp; a Read" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1580849831p2/24156068.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2430209910?book_show_action=true">Sep 16, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christina - Recipe &amp; a Read" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christina - Recipe &amp; a Read" href="/user/show/24156068-christina---recipe-a-read">Christina - Recipe &amp; a Read</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2430209910" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1815191988468630780"><b>3.5 well, lakes and summer camps are now on my shifty list stars!!!!</b><br/><br/><i>Full review along with a recipe for Ratatouille featured on my blog <a href='https://recipeandaread.wordpress.com/2018/09/17/the-last-time-i-lied-review-ratatouille-recipe/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Recipe and a Read</a>!!!</i><br/><br/>When Emma Davis was just 13 years old she attended summer camp at the prestigious Camp Nightingale (known to kids at her school as Camp Rich Bitch). Emma is the last to arrive and the last to leave, what happens in-between is every camper’s worst nightmare. One night, after an argument gone awry Emma’s three cabin mates (Vivian, Natalie and A</span>
  <span id="freeText1815191988468630780" style="display:none"><b>3.5 well, lakes and summer camps are now on my shifty list stars!!!!</b><br /><br /><i>Full review along with a recipe for Ratatouille featured on my blog <a href="https://recipeandaread.wordpress.com/2018/09/17/the-last-time-i-lied-review-ratatouille-recipe/" rel="nofollow noopener">Recipe and a Read</a>!!!</i><br /><br />When Emma Davis was just 13 years old she attended summer camp at the prestigious Camp Nightingale (known to kids at her school as Camp Rich Bitch). Emma is the last to arrive and the last to leave, what happens in-between is every camper’s worst nightmare. One night, after an argument gone awry Emma’s three cabin mates (Vivian, Natalie and Alison) sneak out – never to be heard from or seen again. Vanishing into thin air.<br /><br /><b>Everything is a game, Em. Whether you know it or not. Which means that sometimes a lie is more than just a lie. Sometimes, it’s the only way to win.</b><br /><br />Now 15 years later Emma is gaining notoriety for her art work. Little do her adoring new fans know – this is a lesson in obsession. An inability to let the past go. Emma can only paint one thing: Camp Nightingale and the 3 girls forever vanishing into the woods. To say she obsesses over the girls and their ultimate demise is the understatement of the century. It is an all-consuming need that shapes Emma and her life from the moment she entered the camp and it has never relinquished its grip. <br />When former Camp Nightingale owner Francesca Harris-White (Franny) approaches and purchases one of Emma’s paintings and asks to have lunch, Emma can’t help her weary curiosity. Franny is here to offer Emma a job. Fifteen years after the closing of Camp Nightingale, Franny wishes to reopen its doors with a new mission to allow girls in based on merit instead of wealth and she wants Emma to be a painting instructor. <br /><br /><b>So much water. So much land. So many places to disappear.</b><br /><br />Sager is a true master of suspense building. While he’s fallen to a lot of typical thriller/mystery topes (unreliable narrator, suspicious wealthy family hiding secrets) he brings a fresh take to these over-done story lines and builds a need within the reader to race to the finish. This one won’t have you wanting to skim just to get to the “who dunnit” at the end but rather savor the pieces and clues that Sager delves out with a deft hand. <br /><br />In the end there are ultimately two back-to-back bombshells that are dropped on the reader fairly close together. What I’ll give <i>The Last Time I Lied</i> is that it’s one of the most surprised I’ve been in reading a thriller in a long time. However, while surprise is generally the end goal of a mystery – it doesn’t always mean its well done. Sager’s writing is unceasingly well-done, his prose are detailed and bright. However, I was left here disappointed in the development into the final twists and the ultimate ending. It felt to me a bit out of left field and the penultimate twist felt disconnected to the web that Sager wove and I was hoping for something deeper from it. <br /><br /><b>Sometimes a lie is more than just a lie. Sometimes it's the only way to win.</b><br /><br />Despite a few misgivings I really enjoyed this edge-of-your-seat thriller and I’m thrilled to have found such an amazing author whose future books I’ll immediately be picking up. The writing is top notch and the suspense is thick and heavy throughout. While many of the characters weren’t particularly likeable Sager shows that isn’t always necessary to create a gripping read that once you sink your teeth into – you won’t be able to step away.<br /><br /><i>I completed this as a Traveling Friends read and it was a real treat to discuss with others!</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="1815191988468630780" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2532335890" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2532335890" />
    <a title="Melanie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie"><img alt="Melanie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577914102p2/3030788.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2532335890?book_show_action=true">Sep 30, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melanie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melanie" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie">Melanie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=buddy-reads">buddy-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2532335890" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9090572347685700085"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1540497806i/26501725._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“So much water. So much land. So many places to disappear.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><i>The Last Time I Lied</i> was such a fun book to read during this spooky season. It really kept me on the edge of my seat, it was so thrilling, it was so chillingly atmospheric, and that ending was really unpredictable. I’m so happy I picked this book up this October! Also, to everyone who participated with us in <a href='https://meltotheany.com/2018/09/24/fridayfrightathon-2018/' rel='nofollow noopener'>#FridayFrightAThon</a>, thank you so much! It was such an honor to read alongside so many of you! And hopefully this last b</span>
  <span id="freeText9090572347685700085" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1540497806i/26501725._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“So much water. So much land. So many places to disappear.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><i>The Last Time I Lied</i> was such a fun book to read during this spooky season. It really kept me on the edge of my seat, it was so thrilling, it was so chillingly atmospheric, and that ending was really unpredictable. I’m so happy I picked this book up this October! Also, to everyone who participated with us in <a href="https://meltotheany.com/2018/09/24/fridayfrightathon-2018/" rel="nofollow noopener">#FridayFrightAThon</a>, thank you so much! It was such an honor to read alongside so many of you! And hopefully this last book helped you get into the Halloween mood! <br><br>This is a story about a twenty-eight-year-old woman named Emma, who is still haunted by something that happened fifteen-years ago at summer camp. In present day, she is an artist that is finally having her first gallery event. But the thing is, all the inspiration for all the paintings at the showing were also inspired by what happened when she was thirteen-years-old. <br><br>Fifteen-years ago, Emma went to summer camp late and was forced to bunk with three older girls in a cabin. She quickly becomes close with one of them, Vivian, who treats her like a little sister. But she soon finds out that Vivian was keeping secrets from her. Yet, Emma never found out what those secrets were, because one morning she wakes up and the three girls are missing and are never to be found again. <br><br>This story is told with flashbacks constantly showing us what really happened all those years ago. And we slowly find out why Emma is unable to paint anything but those three missing girls. But Emma is offered some closure, when she is asked to go back to the camp, to teach art, and to maybe receive some semblance of closure for herself and for her art. <br><br>But once she goes back to Camp Nightingale, she learns that some people’s lives never went back to normal after that haunting morning. And Emma also realizes that some people aren’t going to let her forget that they blame her for whatever happened. <br><br>Again, this was so much fun to read. I was so surprised at how many different directions this story was able to take, and how I never saw which way the story was going. I also think the second person point of views were really well done and distributed throughout the story for the perfect amount. I honestly never wanted to put this book down. <br><br>But, not to get into spoiler territory, I hated the epilogue. Well, I loved and hated the epilogue. I actually think the last twist was such a work of genius. But I was absolutely appalled at the way Emma handled it. Therefore, the book was kind of left off on a sour note for me, sadly. <br><br>Overall, I really did enjoy this one. I loved going along with Emma and solving the present-day mystery and the mystery of the past at the same time. And, seriously, the summer camp setting was so perfectly spooky. I think I’m just a bit of a harsh rater with thrillers, honestly. But if you’re looking for something that you won’t be able to predict, and that will put you in a scary mood, I completely recommend this! <br><br>Lastly, something I want to bring up that in no way impacts my rating; I really do not like how this male author writes under a female sounding pseudonym. I also don’t like how there is no author picture and the author note and acknowledgements makes an effort to not have the reader know this story is written by a man. I get that Gillian Flynn was (maybe still is) the thriller queen for a while, but it just makes me feel grossed out that I feel like he is hiding that he is a man to try to sell more. Because white men don’t have it easy enough, you know? <br><br><a href="https://meltotheany.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/meltotheany/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.twitter.com/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://meltotheany.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UC4RbHEg_fH6CewJrh_0xJ9g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="http://www.twitch.tv/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitch</a> <br><br><b>Content and trigger warnings</b> for schizophreniform, anxiety attacks, loss of a loved one, alcoholism, slut shaming (a lot), peeping toms, many fatphobic comments, negative comments about food, talk of cancer, and sex between a sixteen-year-old and nineteen-year-old. <br><br>Buddy read for <a href="https://meltotheany.com/2018/09/24/fridayfrightathon-2018/" rel="nofollow noopener">#FridayFrightAThon</a> which I co-hosted with <a href="https://acourtofcrownsandquills.wordpress.com/2018/09/23/blanca-y-roja-by-anna-marie-mclemore/" rel="nofollow noopener">Amy @ A Court of Crowns and Quills</a>, <a href="https://pinotandpages247.wordpress.com/2018/09/23/arc-review-shadow-of-the-fox/" rel="nofollow noopener">Jen @ Pinot and Pages</a>, &amp; <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=otwtCWoDoNs" rel="nofollow noopener">Chelsea @ Chelsea Palmer</a>! 👻</span>
  <a data-text-id="9090572347685700085" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <strong>Have you ever played Two Truths and A Lie?</strong>

Her three bunk mates sneak out one night leaving her alone. Something goes wrong and they never return.
